VIEWER CHANGE, 2026-07-16 -- MOBILE RESPONSIVENESS, requested by Michiko: "can you make the names database responsive on mobile." Clarified scope via AskUserQuestion first: (1) full touch support for the interactive graph (drag-to-pan, pinch-to-zoom, tap-to-select, tap-and-hold to drag a node), and (2) the left sidebar and right detail panel become full-screen slide-in drawer overlays on mobile (canvas gets the full screen by default) rather than a stacked/scrollable layout. Both approved.
DRAWERS: added a hamburger #menuBtn (opens #left as a fixed-position slide-in overlay via CSS transform, with its own #leftClose button) and wrapped the existing #right detail panel in a new #rightPanel wrapper (a persistent #rightClose button sits next to it, safe from being wiped out by the `right.innerHTML=h` writes select()/selectEvent()/selectOrg() already do -- #rightPanel uses display:contents on desktop so it's invisible to the existing flex layout, and becomes the slide-in container only below the 860px breakpoint). Added a shared #drawerBackdrop overlay and a #detailFab ("Details") floating button that reopens the right drawer once it's closed, shown only on mobile. select()/selectEvent()/selectOrg() now call openRightDrawer() on mobile right after populating #right (guarded by a window._suppressAutoOpen flag so the automatic initial-load selection doesn't yank the drawer open over the graph before the person has tapped anything); the #plist click handler closes the left drawer after a selection on mobile. New mobile-only CSS (@media max-width:860px) also shrinks/repositions the header, #allbtn, #legend, #hint, and turns #miniPanel into a bottom-sheet with its resize grip hidden (dragging to resize doesn't make sense on a touchscreen sheet).
TOUCH: refactored the existing mousedown/mousemove/mouseup drag-vs-click/rotate/pan logic (already carefully tuned this week to fix the "nodes move on click" bug) into shared pointerDown/pointerMove/pointerUp functions, so touch input reuses the EXACT same interaction logic instead of a parallel implementation that could drift out of sync the same way the mouseup simTTL bug did. Added touchstart/touchmove/touchend/touchcancel listeners on the main canvas: single-finger drag/tap goes through pointerDown/Move/Up unchanged; two-finger touchmove drives pinch-to-zoom (scales view.k against the initial pinch distance); double-tap (two releases within 320ms and 20px) mirrors the desktop dblclick-releases-a-pinned-node behavior via a new shared releasePinAt() helper. touch-action:none added to canvas CSS so the browser never fights these listeners with native scroll/pinch-zoom. The mini ego-panel's existing click listener already handles taps via the browser's native synthetic click-from-tap, so no new JS was needed there.
NOTE: a concurrent session was evidently working the same request in parallel and landed a complementary improvement directly into pipeline/viewer_template.html mid-session -- an isTouchDevice flag (set true on first touchstart) that widens pick()/pickMini()'s hit-radius from 6px to 20px on touch, giving fingers a bigger effective tap target without changing how anything looks. No conflict: it layered in cleanly alongside the pointerDown/Move/Up refactor above. Both changes are present in this build.
TESTING: extended deep_test.js with a new check (5c) that fires REAL touchstart+jitter-touchmove+touchend events (not just calling select() directly) and asserts the same click-stability guarantee 5b already proved for mouse -- zero position drift, zero simTTL wake, correct mini-panel population -- plus a pinch-to-zoom check (view.k increases when two fingers spread apart, without ever touching the main map or opening the mini panel). First iteration of this test was flaky (occasionally resolved to a different node than expected) -- root cause was the test computing its "ground truth" pick() call before isTouchDevice flips true, then comparing against the real touchstart's pick() call which uses the wider 20px padding once isTouchDevice is true; fixed by setting isTouchDevice=true in the test before computing ground truth, matching how a real touch session behaves (stays "touch" for its duration). Not an app bug. Both the mandatory smoke test and the extended deep test (now including 5c) passed cleanly, repeated across several runs with different random layouts.
DEPLOYMENT: rebuilt on the current DB (post run #35b merges, 10,811 people) after re-verifying GitHub HEAD (7cb89cb, unchanged) and the Drive template hadn't moved again right before the final build. Drive copy of index.html/1838_black_metropolis_viewer.html wrote cleanly this time (no repeat of the earlier persistent lock issue). Pushed to GitHub via a lightweight sparse checkout (pipeline/ only, skipping the multi-hundred-MB pages/ocr_text/census directories that made full clones repeatedly time out this session) -- see tail note for the commit hash once pushed.
NEXT: Michiko to try the live site on her phone -- open the left list via the new hamburger button, tap a person/event/org to confirm the detail panel slides in from the right (and the Details button reopens it if she swipes/taps it closed), and confirm drag-to-pan, pinch-to-zoom, and tap-to-select feel right on the "all connections" map. No visual mobile-browser testing tool was available in this session, so this is unverified on a real device.

VIEWER CHANGE, 2026-07-15 -- FIXED NODES STILL MOVING ON CLICK (real root cause this time), + mini-panel resize handle, requested by Michiko: "well I think that we need to have the all connections nodes stop moving when you click on them" -- reported AFTER the mini-panel redesign had already shipped, meaning the earlier fix (stopping select()/selectEvent()/selectOrg() from injecting nodes into the main map) hadn't actually solved it. Root cause this time: the mouseup handler had its OWN separate, unconditional `window._simTTL = Math.max(...,40)` wake that fired on ANY node click in full view -- not just actual drag-releases -- completely independent of select()'s own logic. mousedown sets dragN for every node click (click or drag alike, since it can't know yet which one it'll turn out to be), so that line woke the whole simulation for 40 frames after every plain click, letting the group-anchor/leash/spring forces nudge the settled map each time. My previous deep test only ever called select()/selectEvent()/selectOrg() directly, which never exercises the actual mousedown/mousemove/mouseup DOM event chain at all -- a real gap that let this specific bug through undetected.
FIX: gated that simTTL wake on `!wasClick` (matching the sibling pin-logic line right above it, which already had the correct guard). Also found and fixed a secondary contributor: the elastic-drag mousemove handler can nudge the clicked node's x/y/z by a pixel or two from ordinary mouse/trackpad jitter even on what ends up being a plain click (before wasClick is evaluated at mouseup) -- now the node's exact pre-click position is captured on mousedown and snapped back on mouseup if wasClick is true, so a genuine click never moves the node at all.
ALSO (separate small request from Michiko): "it would be nice to be able to expand and contract the window that shows the detail" -- added a resize handle (bottom-right corner grip, standard nwse-resize cursor) to the mini ego-panel, remembered across visits via localStorage the same way the main #right detail panel's width already is. Restructured #miniPanel to a flex column layout so the canvas grows/shrinks to fill whatever size it's resized to.
ALSO bumped LEASH_RADIUS 1100->1400: caught mid-work that the dataset's continued growth (609 people in the default core view, up from ~500 a few sessions ago) had pushed the well-connected main mass's own natural spread past the old radius (hit 1124), which would have made the leash wrongly start engaging on ordinary, well-connected nodes rather than just the isolated islands it's meant for.
TESTING: upgraded the deep test's DOM stub so addEventListener/removeEventListener on canvas/window elements actually capture and can replay real listeners (previously a total no-op) -- added a new check that fires a REAL mousedown+jitter-mousemove+mouseup sequence (not a direct select() call) and asserts zero position drift, zero simTTL wake, and correct mini-panel population, using pick() itself as ground truth for which node the click resolves to (robust against legitimate node overlaps on a dense 800+-node map, which caused one false-start iteration of this test that was a test-design issue, not an app bug). This is exactly the class of test that would have caught the mouseup regression on the first pass, so future click-related bugs in the real event-handling code path should get caught before shipping now. Both the mandatory smoke test and the extended deep test passed cleanly.
DEPLOYMENT NOTE: hit an unusually persistent (~20+ minute) "Resource deadlock avoided" lock specifically on index.html/1838_black_metropolis_viewer.html on Drive during this push -- other files (including github_token.txt, org_aliases.json, issue_urls.json, smoke_test.js) hit the same transient lock briefly and cleared after a Grep-based hydration retry, but these two large files stayed locked well past that. GitHub HEAD never moved during this window (confirmed via repeated fresh clones), ruling out a genuine concurrent push race -- most likely another session or a local Drive desktop sync client was actively re-uploading these exact files. Given GitHub Pages (not the Drive copy) is what actually serves the live map, pushed straight to GitHub as commit 8a56db9 (verified via fresh clone + git cat-file) without waiting further on the Drive copy, which should be retried once the lock clears.
NEXT: Michiko to confirm clicking a node in "all connections" view now leaves everything else completely still (should be truly fixed this time, verified via a real mouse-event simulation, not just the app logic), and that the mini panel's new resize grip works as expected. If the Drive copy of index.html/1838_black_metropolis_viewer.html still looks stale, a future session should just retry the plain `cp` from a fresh rebuild -- the GitHub-hosted live site is already current.

VIEWER CHANGE, 2026-07-14 -- FREEZE THE MAIN MAP ON CLICK, ADD MINI EGO-PANEL, requested by Michiko: "when you click in the center all the ball start moving again we need that to be stable ... instead of doing that keep all the ball stable, but let's put a small window in the top right that opens up ... shows that node with all of its connections that way we can keep the center clear and the clusters will be more visible." Correctly diagnosed the root cause herself: clicking a person/org/event used to call ensurePersonInFull/ensureEventInFull/ensureOrgInFull, which injected that entity's full real connections directly into the shared main-map nodes/links array and set window._simTTL to wake the simulation -- but since forces like the group-anchor and leash (both added earlier this week) recompute over the WHOLE node set every frame, adding even a few new nodes anywhere shifted the equilibrium for EVERY already-settled node, not just the clicked area, reading as the whole map jiggling.
FIX: removed ensurePersonInFull/ensureEventInFull/ensureOrgInFull and personMap() entirely -- the main map is now NEVER mutated by a click. select()/selectEvent()/selectOrg() in full-view mode now only (a) highlight the clicked node's existing on-map links if it happens to already be visible, and (b) call a new openMiniPanel(), which builds that node's COMPLETE real ego-network (every actual neighbor/attendee/member, not limited by the default FULL_MIN_CONN density filter) into a small floating panel top-right of the canvas. This reuses the exact same, already-proven standalone ego-view logic (buildGraph/buildEventGraph/buildOrgGraph, same physics, same 300-iteration settle) via a snapshot-and-restore wrapper (snapshotEgo()) that temporarily swaps the shared nodes/links/view globals, runs the builder into a throwaway result, then restores the main map's saved state completely untouched. The mini panel gets its own small canvas (#miniCv), its own simplified static draw routine (drawMini(), fit-to-bounds via fitMiniView() since ego networks vary wildly in size), a close button, and click-to-navigate on any node inside it (which just calls select()/selectEvent()/selectOrg() again, recursing naturally). Toggling out of "all connections" mode now also closes the mini panel.
TESTING: rewrote the deep test's click-behavior section entirely -- it now asserts the main map's node COUNT, link COUNT, and every node's actual x/y/z POSITION are unchanged (down to <1px, real result 0.000px) after clicking a person with real hidden connections, and that window._simTTL stays at 0 (the sim never wakes). Separately asserts the mini panel gets exactly the correct real ego-network: for a person, the top-40-by-weight real neighbors (same cap the standalone ego view has always used), independently recomputed and compared 1:1; for an event/org, ALL real attendees/members with no cap. Also verified closeMiniPanel() clears its own state without touching the main map. Both the mandatory smoke test and the rewritten deep test passed cleanly.

VIEWER CHANGE, 2026-07-13 (same day, fourth follow-up) -- GROUP-ANCHOR FORCE, orgs/events pulled toward their OWN members' centroid, flagged by Michiko from two more screenshots showing "Institute for Colored You[th]..." still sitting far from its ~20-27 members with long lines, even after the leash fix above shipped. Diagnosis (via a targeted diag script run directly against the live deployed viewer): the leash only engages when a node exceeds LEASH_RADIUS from the map's GLOBAL centroid -- but this org (837px from centroid) and its 27 members (306-512px from centroid) were each individually within that radius, just on different sides of it, so their pairwise distance stayed large. Root cause: this org has ZERO members for whom it's their PRIMARY affiliation (all 27 are "secondary"), so it only had ~27 weak (0.0025 stiffness) springs pulling toward scattered targets and nothing strong anchoring it near where its members actually clustered.
FIX: new direct per-frame force in tick() (full map only) -- for every org/event node, compute the live centroid of its own currently-linked members each frame and pull toward it directly (new GROUP_ANCHOR_K constant, calibrated to 0.03: high enough to meaningfully help, but pushing further gained little more ground while risking the well-connected main mass itself exceeding LEASH_RADIUS). Real result on the flagged org: 837px-from-centroid/big-pairwise-gap down to ~320px from its own members' actual centroid; the dataset's worst case (a 42-member org with zero primary members) settled at ~270px, down from 800px+.
TESTING: extended the deep test with a new check that finds a real org with >=5 members and zero primary affiliations, lets the sim settle, and asserts its distance from its own members' live centroid stays under a threshold calibrated against the real data (350px). Also re-verified the existing leash/primary-affiliation/drift checks still pass at the chosen GROUP_ANCHOR_K (max default-view distance from centroid 1041-1083px, comfortably under LEASH_RADIUS=1100). Both the mandatory smoke test and the extended deep test passed cleanly. Hit a disk-nearly-full sandbox (307M free) mid-verification from accumulated /tmp clones across this session's many pushes -- cleared old scratch clones to recover 3.3G before the final verify-clone succeeded. Every frame, compute the map's overall centroid; anything further than LEASH_RADIUS gets pulled back proportional to the overshoot. Nodes within the radius (the normal well-connected main mass) are completely unaffected -- calibrated against the real dataset, which sits within ~900-960 units of centroid on its own (p99), so 1100 gives it comfortable room before ever engaging.

VIEWER CHANGE, 2026-07-13 (same day, second follow-up) -- FIXED NEWLY-REVEALED PEOPLE DRIFTING FAR AWAY, flagged by Michiko from a live screenshot showing long lines shooting out to isolated people scattered across (and off) the screen after clicking to reveal hidden connections, instead of those people clustering in close as intended. Root cause: the primary-affiliation push (below) deliberately made person-to-person link physics weak (stiffness 0.0012, target up to ~980px) so they wouldn't compete with the new org/event-anchored layout -- correct reasoning for the ~495 already-visible core people (who have a strong primary-affiliation spring anchoring them elsewhere anyway), but wrong for a freshly-revealed person created on click, who usually belongs to no tracked org/event at all and has NO other force acting on them. Their only connection is that one weak, long-target spring, so ambient repulsion from the hundreds of other nearby nodes flung them outward before the weak spring could react, stranding them far from wherever they were pulled in. Fixed by replacing the loose weight-based target with a fixed short one (new PP_GAP_BASE=40px * spacing) and raising stiffness to 0.015 -- strong enough to win against repulsion and keep a freshly-revealed person close, while staying below the primary org/event tier (0.02) so it doesn't override that anchoring for people who do have one.
TESTING: extended the deep test to simulate the ~90-frame settle window draw() would normally run after revealing a hidden person, then measure their actual distance from whoever revealed them -- real result: 144px (down from effectively unbounded before). Bonus: the primary-vs-secondary affiliation separation from the change below also got tighter as a side effect (105px vs 451px average, ~4.3x, up from ~2x). Both the mandatory smoke test and the deep test passed cleanly. Rebuilt from the same DB/GitHub state as the immediately preceding push (no concurrent drift), pushed as commit c8691ad on top of 8b63b80, verified via fresh clone + md5sum, copied back to Drive (index.html/1838_black_metropolis_viewer.html, md5-verified).
NEXT: Michiko to eyeball the live map again -- clicking a person should now reveal their real connections clustered close by, not stretched across the screen. PP_GAP_BASE and its stiffness (0.015) are the levers if it still needs adjusting, right next to PRIMARY_GAP_BASE/SECONDARY_GAP_BASE near the top of the graph script.

VIEWER CHANGE, 2026-07-13 (same day, follow-up) -- ANCHOR PEOPLE TO THEIR PRIMARY ORG/EVENT AFFILIATION, requested by Michiko after the edge-visibility decluttering below looked better but she wanted the spatial layout itself to carry more meaning: "have the people balls closer into the event or org balls. Those linked to multiple events and orgs will then stick out as connectors. Those linked to only one or two will be closer in and look like a cluster... closest to the org or event with the largest number of connections."
DESIGN: new personPrimaryAffil()/isPrimaryAffil() helpers (cached, computed once) determine for every person which single org or event they belong to has the largest real total membership/attendance (comparing across both together) -- that's their "primary" affiliation. Every person-org and person-event link, wherever it's created (buildFullGraph, ensurePersonInFull, ensureOrgInFull, ensureEventInFull), is now tagged link.primary accordingly. tick()'s physics for the full map treat primary vs secondary very differently: a primary link gets both a short target distance (PRIMARY_GAP_BASE=26px * spacing) AND a much stiffer spring (0.02 vs the old flat 0.004) so a person actually pulls in tight against their main group despite ambient repulsion from the hundreds of other nearby nodes; a secondary affiliation link (any OTHER org/event the same person also belongs to) stays loose (SECONDARY_GAP_BASE=140px, stiffness 0.0025). Net effect: people in just one or two groups nestle in close and read as part of that cluster; people who bridge several groups get stretched between them and visibly stick out as connectors -- directly reflecting how central they are to the network. Person-to-person links (already hidden by default from the prior change) were also given a weaker stiffness (0.0012) so they don't fight this new org/event-anchored layout.
CAUGHT MID-TUNING: the first pass only shortened the target distance and left stiffness uniform across all link types -- the deep test's distance measurement showed the effect was real but weak (primary links averaging 382px vs secondary 461px, only a 1.2x difference, too subtle to read visually). Diagnosed that ambient repulsion from the hundreds of other nodes on the map was overwhelming a merely-short target at the default spring stiffness. Fixed by differentiating STIFFNESS too, not just target distance -- re-tested and got primary avg 231px vs secondary avg 478px, a clean ~2x separation, which should read clearly on the live map.
TESTING: extended the deep test with checks that every person has at most one link flagged primary, that the flagging matches an independent recomputation of each person's real largest org/event membership (spot-checked against a real multi-affiliated person in the dataset), and that after the full 260-iteration presettle, primary-affiliation links measurably average a shorter real x/y/z distance than secondary ones. Both the mandatory smoke test and the deep test passed cleanly. Rebuilt from the same DB/GitHub state as the immediately preceding push (no concurrent-session drift this round), pushed as commit d07644a on top of e659202, verified via fresh clone + md5sum, copied back to Drive (index.html/1838_black_metropolis_viewer.html, md5-verified).
NEXT: Michiko to eyeball the live map -- people should now visibly nestle around whichever org/event dominates their real-world affiliation, with multi-affiliated "bridge" people readably stretched between clusters. If the clustering still isn't tight enough or the stick-out effect isn't pronounced enough, PRIMARY_GAP_BASE/SECONDARY_GAP_BASE and their stiffness values (0.02 / 0.0025) are the levers, all named near the top of the graph script in viewer_template.html, right after the groupR definitions.

VIEWER CHANGE, 2026-07-13 -- REPLACED CLUSTER-BUBBLE COLLAPSING WITH EDGE-VISIBILITY DECLUTTERING, requested by Michiko after reviewing a live screenshot of the cluster-bubble version (previous entry below): "let's try making the events and organizations larger based on number of connections ... keep all the people uniform size ... remove the part where the people don't show until you click on a bubble -- they will always show ... only show lines between the person and the event or the person and the organization, not person to person until you click on a person, and then you can see the lines they have to other people." This is a full pivot away from the cluster-bubble design tried earlier today -- that whole mechanism (CLUSTER_MIN_SIZE/MAX_CLUSTER_SIZE/clusterR, the balanced-LPA community collapsing + recursive re-splitting, resolvePersonNode/registerPersonNode/explodeCluster, the cluster click-dispatch/legend/hint text) is REMOVED. Every core person (10+ connections, the existing FULL_MIN_CONN filter) is individually visible again, same as before clustering existed.
NEW DESIGN: (1) org/event nodes now get one of THREE fixed sizes based on real total people count instead of two -- Small (<=10), Medium (11-20), Large (21+); GROUP_R_SMALL/MEDIUM/LARGE (8/12/17px) replace the old two-tier GROUP_SIZE_THRESHOLD/GROUP_R_NORMAL/GROUP_R_LARGE. (2) person nodes are now ALL one uniform size (PERSON_R=8, same value as the org/event Small tier) -- dot size no longer tries to encode a person's importance. (3) THE KEY CHANGE: person-to-person lines -- the actual bulk of the line clutter (~5,000 of ~6,300 total links on the current dataset, vs only ~1,300 person-org/person-event links) -- are now hidden by default on the full map and only drawn for whichever person is currently selected/highlighted, revealing their real connections to other people on click. Person-to-org and person-to-event lines always render regardless of selection, since there are far fewer of them and they're what shows organizational/event affiliation at a glance. Ego/org/event drill-down views are unaffected -- only the full "all connections" map changed. Community detection (label propagation) is KEPT, still used for spatial pull only (grouping related people near each other visually), exactly as it was used before clustering was ever introduced.
TESTING: extended the deep test to actually RUN draw() against a live ctx.moveTo call counter (instrumented the canvas-context stub) rather than just inspecting the links[] data model, which intentionally still holds every real link regardless of what's currently rendered -- this verifies the actual on-screen line count, not just the underlying data. Confirmed on the real dataset: with nothing selected, draw() renders exactly the 1,296 non-person-to-person links and none of the 5,032 person-to-person ones; selecting a hub person (id 715, 108 person-to-person links) renders exactly 1,296+108=1,404 lines, i.e. precisely that person's own connections added on top, no one else's. Also verified uniform person sizing and the new three-tier org/event sizing spot-checked against real org member counts. Removed the now-obsolete cluster-bubble assertions from the test. Both the mandatory smoke test and the deep test passed cleanly.

VIEWER CHANGE, 2026-07-12 (same day, third follow-up) -- INTELLIGENT CLUSTERING: COLLAPSE COMMUNITIES INTO CLICK-TO-EXPAND BUBBLES, requested by Michiko after seeing a live screenshot of the frozen/settled map and asking "I wonder if there is an intelligent way to cluster?" -- explicitly not another numeric tuning pass. Real diagnosis this time: the freeze/no-spin fix above was correct but insufficient -- even fully settled and static, ~494 individually-drawn people with ~6,300 edges in one flat pool is just unreadable, a pure information-density problem that no amount of spacing/zoom/motion-freezing can solve. Asked Michiko to choose a direction (AskUserQuestion: cluster bubbles by default / hide edges instead / both); she picked cluster bubbles.
FIX: the label-propagation community detection already used for spatial pull is now used to structurally COLLAPSE the graph -- every detected community of CLUSTER_MIN_SIZE=6+ people becomes ONE sized bubble node (radius scales with real member count) instead of N individual dots, labeled by its best-connected member ("Name + N more"). Clicking a bubble explodes it back into real member nodes with every real connection restored -- to each other, to already-visible nodes, AND to people still hidden in OTHER bubbles (linked to that bubble as a whole, NOT cascade-exploded -- critical, otherwise one click would unravel the whole map back into a hairball). Org/event nodes are untouched, they already had two-tier sizing from the earlier density overhaul.
HIT A REAL SNAG MID-BUILD, CAUGHT BY THE DEEP TEST: plain majority-vote label propagation collapsed ~84% of the 494-person core network into ONE giant 413-person community -- a single "many more" bubble that would just recreate the hairball the instant anyone clicked it, defeating the entire point. Fixed with a standard anti-monster-component technique: bias each node's candidate-label pull by 1/sqrt(that label's current size) during propagation, so already-large communities get progressively less attractive to new joiners ("balanced label propagation"). Also added a MAX_CLUSTER_SIZE=45 cap with recursive re-splitting (same balanced propagation, restricted to just the oversized subgraph, fresh per-node starting labels, up to depth 4) for anything still too big afterward. Result on the real dataset: 413-person super-blob -> 29 well-distributed bubbles ranging 6-49 members each, plus 35 people left individually visible (communities under the 6-person floor aren't worth bubbling). Default full-map node count: 746 (post FULL_MIN_CONN=10 trim, pre-clustering baseline from the earlier density overhaul) -> 316 today.
ARCHITECTURE: new resolvePersonNode()/registerPersonNode() give every ensure*InFull() helper (ensurePersonInFull, ensureOrgInFull, ensureEventInFull) a single cluster-aware source of truth for "whatever node currently represents this person on screen" -- their own real node if shown/expanded, or their bubble if not. This is what prevents duplicate nodes and cascade-exploding: an org/event/person that links to someone still hidden in a bubble just draws a link TO the bubble, it doesn't force it open. Selecting/searching a specific person still hidden in a bubble explodes exactly THEIR bubble and highlights them specifically (not an arbitrary bubble-mate) via a small ensurePersonInFull top-of-function check. Legend and the full-view hint text updated (dashed blue-gray circle = group, click to open).
TESTING: extended the same deep test (evals the built script, invokes real functions against the real dataset) with new checks: bubble count/size distribution logged, every bubble respects the CLUSTER_MIN_SIZE floor and CLUSTER_R_MIN/MAX radius bounds, every one of the 494 core people is accounted for as either an individual node or exactly one bubble member (none dropped), exploding a bubble restores full real connectivity for every member (verified against the real NBR adjacency, not just link count), exploding one bubble leaves every other bubble completely untouched (explicit no-cascade regression guard), and clicking/selecting a person still hidden in a bubble explodes exactly their bubble and returns their specific node. Caught and fixed two test-design bugs along the way (not product bugs): the "missing neighbor" check needed to use the new cluster-aware resolvePersonNode() instead of a plain individual-node lookup, since a real connection to someone still in a bubble is correctly represented as a link to that bubble, not a dangling reference; and the node-count-after-explosion check needed >= instead of strict equality, since exploding a bubble also pulls in each member's real neighbors below FULL_MIN_CONN that never had a node at all -- by design, identical to how a normal single-person-click expansion already worked. Both the mandatory smoke test and the fully-extended deep test passed cleanly on the final build. Rebuilt from the same DB as the prior three pushes today (md5 f6a0fab84f5667c7d30e3a853611a397, unchanged, re-verified immediately before the push -- no concurrent-session collision, though the shared pipeline/build_viewer.py session-mount constants WERE found reset to a different session's paths (sleepy-loving-ride) mid-run, confirming another session was active concurrently again -- handled the same safe way as before, patched a fresh local /tmp scratch copy rather than touching the shared file). Pushed as commit 386e0b1 on top of 1b09924, verified via fresh clone + md5sum, copied back to Drive (index.html/1838_black_metropolis_viewer.html, md5-verified).
NEXT: Michiko to eyeball the live "all connections" view again -- default load should now show roughly a few dozen shapes (some individual people, ~29 dashed group bubbles, plus the existing org/event bubbles) instead of a solid hairball core, with each bubble opening into its real members and connections on click. If any single bubble still feels too big/generic on inspection, MAX_CLUSTER_SIZE (currently 45) is the lever to lower; if too many small groups feel fragmented, CLUSTER_MIN_SIZE (currently 6) is the lever to raise. Both are named constants near FULL_MIN_CONN at the top of the graph script in viewer_template.html.

VIEWER CHANGE, 2026-07-12 (same day, second follow-up) -- FREEZE PHYSICS + DISABLE AUTO-SPIN, requested by Michiko after the spacing/zoom tuning above still "looked too crazy" and she asked for better design thinking rather than more numeric tweaking. Diagnosis: the real culprit wasn't spacing at all -- the full-map simulation ticked every single animation frame forever (never truly settling) AND auto-rotated by default (window._spin=true), so even a well-spaced layout looked like it was constantly churning/drifting, which reads as chaos regardless of how far apart nodes are. Fix, all in viewer_template.html's graph script: (1) buildFullGraph() now presettles fully with 260 iterations (up from 160), then explicitly freezes (window._simTTL=0) and defaults auto-spin off (window._spin=false) -- manual drag-to-rotate still works, only the always-on auto-rotation is gone. (2) draw()'s end-of-frame loop now only calls tick() in full view while a node is actively being dragged, or briefly (while window._simTTL>0, decrementing each frame) right after new nodes are pulled in -- otherwise positions are completely static frame to frame. (3) ensurePersonInFull/ensureEventInFull/ensureOrgInFull each set window._simTTL=90 when they add nodes (via clicking to reveal hidden connections), so the newly revealed nodes animate smoothly into place instead of popping in static, then the sim re-freezes. (4) Drag-release (mouseup) and un-pinning (double-click) each give a node's neighbors a 40-frame window to resettle before re-freezing. Ego (non-"all connections") views are unaffected -- they keep their original always-on gentle ticking.
TESTING: extended the same one-off deep test used for the density overhaul (evals the built script, invokes real functions against the real dataset) with new checks: window._spin===false and window._simTTL===0 immediately after buildFullGraph() (before any click-expansion, which intentionally wakes the sim -- had to reorder the check ahead of the expansion test in the script after an initial false-fail from test ordering, not a product bug); expanding a shown person via ensurePersonInFull sets window._simTTL>0. Also logged (informational, not asserted) the residual drift from manually forcing extra tick() calls post-settle -- a physics sim naturally has some residual spring motion even near rest, so the real freeze guarantee is that draw() never calls tick() at all when idle, not that tick() itself produces zero motion if called. Both the mandatory smoke test and the deep test passed cleanly. Rebuilt from the same DB as the previous two pushes (md5 f6a0fab84f5667c7d30e3a853611a397, unchanged, re-verified immediately before AND right before the push -- no concurrent-session collision this run), pushed as commit 703b727 on top of 59d2d87, verified via fresh clone + md5sum, copied back to Drive (index.html/1838_black_metropolis_viewer.html, md5-verified).
NEXT: Michiko to eyeball the live "all connections" view again -- it should now feel calm/static once loaded rather than perpetually moving, with drag-to-rotate and click-to-expand as the only motion. If it still feels dense, the remaining lever is FULL_MIN_CONN/GROUP_SIZE_THRESHOLD (raise either to show fewer default nodes), not spacing/zoom, which is likely tapped out.

GITHUB PUSH -- CAUGHT A REAL HAZARD: a plain `git clone --depth 1` worked fine this run (645M, disk stayed healthy at 3.5G free after -- the disk-space fix appears to have resolved the git-clone-triggered exhaustion documented in earlier runs too, not just the useradd issue). BUT a naive `cp -r <Drive pipeline dir>/. <repo>/pipeline/` to sync the pipeline folder partially FAILED SILENTLY IN A DANGEROUS WAY: for every source file that hit the "Resource deadlock avoided" hydration error mid-copy, cp still created/truncated the DESTINATION file to 0 bytes rather than leaving it untouched -- this would have committed near-total deletions of pipeline/PIPELINE.md, reocr_backfill.md, and several .bak/.tmp files (git diff showed e.g. "PIPELINE.md | 82 ------- " before I caught it) if not caught by inspecting `git status`/`git diff --stat` before committing. CAUGHT AND FIXED: `git checkout HEAD -- <paths>` restored the corrupted-to-0-byte tracked files, and the newly-created 0-byte tmp_chunk_*.txt (untracked, never meant to be committed per standing practice) were deleted outright. FLAGGING FOR ALL FUTURE RUNS: when syncing files from the Drive mount into a git working tree, do NOT bulk `cp -r` an entire directory in one shot -- either hydrate every source file first (Grep-tool trick) and verify the copy succeeded, or copy files individually and check sizes, or at minimum always run `git status`/`git diff --stat` and eyeball it for suspicious large deletions before `git add`/`git commit`. This is a genuinely dangerous footgun, worse than the read-side deadlock errors alone since it fails without raising an exception on the write side.
Final git status after the fix: black_metropolis.db, index.html, progress.txt, 6 pipeline/*.py, issue_urls.json, merge_candidates.md, viewer_template.html modified; extractions30.json + 6 ocr_text/*.txt + 8 pages/*.jpg added. Committed and pushed to https://github.com/michiQ/1838Names.git main, excluding github_token.txt as always.

GOLD FOUND (from manual reading, not yet in the DB): a real-time editorial exchange between Freedom's Journal and Mordecai M. Noah's New-York Enquirer -- a pseudonymous correspondent "Mordecai" rebuts Noah's Aug-10-reprinted "The Negroes" article on FJ_1827-08-17 p3, and the very next issue (FJ_1827-08-24 p3-4) runs an unsigned Cornish & Russwurm editorial "MAJOR NOAH'S 'NEGROES'" that explicitly credits "our correspondent Mordecai" with having already answered Noah's charge that free Black New Yorkers are "a nuisance incomparably greater than a million of slaves." Also: a new "OBSERVER" pseudonymous column debuts across three installments (Nos. I-III) in these two issues; a New Haven travel-letter installment describing a sparsely-attended Freedom's Journal subscription meeting at the African Meeting-House and discriminatory treatment at a Hartford inn; the American Convention for Promoting the Abolition of Slavery's 20th Biennial Meeting notice (Philadelphia, Oct 2 1827, signed by Secretary Edwin P. 1820 PHILADELPHIA DIRECTORY IMPORTED, 2026-07-10 (new source, not a new-issue-processing run): Michiko produced a new source file outside the usual PDF pipeline -- "1820 Directory - Black Residents (cross-marked).csv" (Google Drive file ID 1SJeZzU8WvnFLs2TSdValbnJJfQJy6sPO, not in the mounted Newspapers folder), her cross-marked (dagger symbol) extraction of 1,654 Black residents from the 1820 Philadelphia city directory (First Name/Second Name/Occupation/Address/PDF Page/Confidence/Needs Review/Original OCR Entry columns; directory-style surname-first name order, verified against the Original OCR Entry text). FETCH: the Drive download_file_content tool returned a 271K-character base64 JSON blob too large to load directly (25000-token Read cap); reconstructed it via a subagent doing chunked Grep extraction (~17 x 15-17KB chunks) from the host-side temp file the harness spilled it to, reassembled and base64-decoded via bash, saved as pipeline/1820_directory_source.csv (1655 lines incl. header, 203,347 bytes -- matches the Drive-reported 203KB). KNOWN CLEANUP GAP: the 17 scratch chunk files (pipeline/tmp_chunk_00.txt..16.txt) could not be deleted -- both `rm` and Python `os.remove()` failed with "Operation not permitted" against this Drive mount (a cloud-mount deletion restriction, distinct from the standing /tmp root-owned-leftover hazard); they were excluded from the GitHub sync but still need manual deletion from the Drive pipeline/ folder (by Michiko, or a future session with different delete permissions).
NEW SCRIPT: pipeline/import_1820_directory.py, modeled on import_census.py -- loads the 1,654 rows into a new `directory_1820` table and links each to a person via a new `directory_links(person_id, directory='1820', row_id)` table (same shape as census_links). Matches against Winch people (source='winch') by normalized "given surname", indexing BOTH canonical_name and any confirmed aliases (so previously-merged alternate spellings are matchable) -- a directory row links to a Winch person only when unambiguous (exactly one candidate); everything else (0 or 2+ candidates) becomes a brand-new person tagged source='1820directory'. NEVER auto-merges, per Michiko's standing instruction. ONE DELIBERATE DEVIATION from import_census.py: does NOT dedupe same-name rows within the source into one cached person (census's cidx does this) -- a check of the CSV found 120 rows (~60 name-pairs, e.g. two different "Adams, John" entries, woodsawyer/back 459 south Second vs mariner/84 Gaskill court) sharing a name but with distinct occupation/address and zero identical full rows, i.e. genuinely different people; deduping by name would have silently merged them. Documented in a new "1820 Philadelphia directory" section of PIPELINE.md.
Also updated for the new source: build_viewer.py (attaches a `directory` list -- occupation/address/PDF page/confidence/needs-review/OCR text -- to each linked person, same pattern as census, no graph edges synthesized; added to the not-pruned "keep" condition so directory-only people survive into the viewer); find_merge_candidates.py (now counts directory_links alongside appearances/winch_refs/census_links so directory-sourced people aren't filtered out as noise, and shows directory record counts in candidate descriptions); apply_merges.py (directory_links added to the list of tables reassigned on a confirmed merge). viewer_template.html gained a "1820 directory" filter chip, a new b-d badge/color, blob-search inclusion of occupation/address text, and a detail-panel "1820 city directory" card section (occupation/address/directory page/confidence/needs-review flag/OCR text); MANDATORY smoke test (node pipeline/smoke_test.js) passed on the rebuilt viewer.

GRAPH CIRCLE SIZING 2026-07-09 (5th batch, viewer display change): Michiko asked to "change all circles to size by number of connections" in the interactive network graph. Investigated pipeline/viewer_template.html's graph rendering, which is a hand-rolled canvas force layout (no D3/canvas library) with two separate graph builders: buildGraph() (the default ego view centered on whichever person is selected in the left list) and buildFullGraph() (the "All connections" 3D map, toggled by the allbtn button, with a further "core network" vs. "everyone" density toggle). Found that buildFullGraph already had a partial version of this feature from an earlier session (shipped by b631daa or before): person nodes there were sized by their real per-view link count via r = 3 + min(16, 1.8*sqrt(c)), but event nodes were a fixed r=9 and org nodes a fixed r=8 regardless of how connected they actually were ("events and orgs stay uniform" per the old comment) -- so it wasn't actually "all circles." The ego view (buildGraph) had no degree-based sizing at all: center node fixed r=16, neighbor nodes sized by their raw co-occurrence edge weight to the center only (7+min(6,w), not a true connection count), event nodes fixed r=11. Extracted the existing full-view formula into a new shared helper, sizeByDegree(nodes, links, rMin, rMax, mult), which counts each node's actual links in the `links` array that was just built for that specific rendered view (not the raw global DATA.edges, since events/orgs don't appear in DATA.edges at all -- their "connections" only exist as the links synthesized per-view from event attendance / org membership), then maps degree to radius as rMin + min(rMax-rMin, mult*sqrt(degree)). Sqrt scale chosen (matching the pre-existing convention) so *area* rather than radius scales with degree, keeping hub nodes readably larger without dominating the canvas. Applied uniformly to all three node types (person/event/org) in both graphs: buildFullGraph now calls sizeByDegree(nodes, links, 3, 19, 1.8) (unchanged constants from the pre-existing people-only formula, just extended to cover events and orgs too); buildGraph (ego view) now calls sizeByDegree(nodes, links, 5, 20, 2.6) after all its links are built, with larger constants than the full view since the ego view shows far fewer nodes on screen at once and previously used bigger fixed sizes (16/11) that this should roughly match at typical degrees. Verified real degree distributions before finalizing constants (via a small Node script parsing the built HTML's embedded DATA and replicating both graph-builder functions): full-map person degree ranges 1-148 in "everyone" mode (radius 4.8-19px, only the top ~1% of hub people hit the 19px cap); full-map event/org degree similarly spans single digits up to ~130 for the biggest orgs (e.g. Philadelphia African Lodge, 131 members). Ego-view spot-checks: a very well-connected person (e.g. James Forten Jr., 47 links) renders their center node at the 20px cap same as before's fixed 16px (now slightly larger, appropriately, since they're a genuine hub); an isolated person with no other connections renders as a single 5px node (previously would have still been a fixed 16px "hub" with nothing around it). Confirmed nothing else needed updating for consistency: this codebase's click hit-testing (pick()), label vertical offset, and circle drawing all already read n.r dynamically rather than hardcoding the old fixed constants, so they adapted automatically; the repulsion/collision physics (repulse()/tick()) in this hand-rolled force layout was already weight-based (spring rest-length keyed off link weight, generic repulsion keyed off a fixed cutoff distance) rather than radius-based, so no separate "collision radius" parameter existed to update. This was a display-layer-only change -- black_metropolis.db was NOT touched and pipeline/build_viewer.py did not need any edits (its DB/template paths were already correct from the prior run); only pipeline/viewer_template.html changed, then build_viewer.py was rerun to regenerate the HTML: 9,206 people, 173 events, 405 articles, 6,485 edges, 195 orgs -- all identical to the prior run's counts, confirming no data changed. Smoke test (node pipeline/smoke_test.js) passed (both script blocks OK). Copied the rebuilt viewer HTML to both filenames and the modified viewer_template.html back to Drive; did not need to copy build_viewer.py back since it was never modified, and did not copy black_metropolis.db back since it was never modified (md5-verified identical). GitHub: verified Drive and GitHub were in sync at start (fresh clone HEAD b631daa, md5-identical to Drive's index.html and black_metropolis.db) before touching anything; pushed as commit ff9d884 (parent b631daa) with index.html and pipeline/viewer_template.html only; post-push fresh clone verified GitHub's index.html is md5-identical to Drive's, the pushed viewer_template.html contains the new sizeByDegree() function, and github_token.txt was not committed. ORG MERGE MECHANISM ADDED 2026-07-09 (4th batch, organizations not people): Michiko sent viewer screenshots of the organizations dropdown showing several spelling variants of the same org listed separately with their own mention/member counts, and asked for both a merge and an organization search. Investigated how org names get into the system first, since there was no known merge mechanism for them: organizations are NOT a DB table with IDs (unlike people) -- they are computed fresh every build_viewer.py run from four free-text sources: (1) winch_references.note via a role-based regex (ORG_RE, "Secretary of the X Society" etc.), (2) appearances.context via a proximity regex (ORG_CTX_RE), (3) the newspaper_orgs DB table (person_id, org TEXT, issue, page) which match_names.py rebuilds from raw OCR text every run via its own regex pass, and (4) events.name when it contains org-flavored keywords (Society/Church/etc). All four funnel through a single choke point, add_org(pid, raw) in build_viewer.py, which cleans the string (org_clean) and dedupes by lowercased label into org_members{}; orgs with >=2 distinct member people survive into DATA.orgs and populate the "All organizations..." dropdown as "Name (member count)". Built a new alias mechanism at that choke point, analogous in spirit to people's merges.json/apply_merges.py but implemented as a pure display-layer normalization since orgs aren't DB rows: pipeline/org_aliases.json is a curated list of {canonical, aliases[], note} groups; build_viewer.py loads it into ORG_ALIAS_LOOKUP (keyed by whitespace-collapsed lowercased string) and add_org() now looks up the cleaned label in that map before computing the dedup key, folding any listed alias into its canonical spelling. Applied Michiko's 4 confirmed groups: (1) "Coachman's Benevolent Society" -> "Coachmen's Benevolent Society" (29 members after merge); (2) "A. M. E. Church" / "A.M. E. Church" / "A.M.E Church" -> "A.M.E. Church" (10 members; note several other org strings like "Eighth General Conference of the A.M.E. Church" legitimately contain the substring and were correctly left as distinct orgs, not folded in); (3) "Female Vigilance Committee" / "Female Vigilant Association" -> "Female Vigilant Committee" (15 members, kept as canonical per Michiko's instruction to prefer the highest-count wording); (4) "Humane Mechanics' Society" -> "Humane Mechanics Society" (11 members). Verified post-build that none of the 7 alias strings remain as separate entries in DATA.orgs. Also added the requested organization search: a new #orgsearch text input above the organizations dropdown in viewer_template.html, mirroring the existing #search person-name box -- it does a case-insensitive substring filter over the dropdown's option list (rebuilding <option> elements on each keystroke via a new renderOrgOptions() function), while preserving the active org filter selection even if it's momentarily filtered out of view. Routine maintenance: pipeline/*.py (apply_merges.py, build_viewer.py, find_merge_candidates.py, import_census.py, load_extractions.py, match_names.py) had stale DB paths from the prior run's sandbox (/tmp/merge3/); repointed to this session's /tmp/org1/ (build_viewer.py's OUT path too); session-mount paths were already correct for this session (charming-magical-davinci). Verified Drive and GitHub were in sync at start (fresh clone HEAD ed97357, md5-identical to Drive's black_metropolis.db and index.html) before touching anything. This was a display-layer-only change -- black_metropolis.db was NOT touched (no import_census/match_names/load_extractions/apply_merges rerun needed, confirmed by md5: DB identical before/after), so only build_viewer.py was rerun: 195 orgs with >=2 members (down slightly from 202, as expected from the 4 merges), 9,206 people, 173 events, 405 articles, 6,485 edges -- all unchanged from the prior run except the org count. Smoke test (node pipeline/smoke_test.js) passed (both script blocks OK). Copied the rebuilt viewer HTML to both filenames, plus org_aliases.json, build_viewer.py, and viewer_template.html back to Drive; did not need to copy black_metropolis.db back since it was never modified. GitHub pushed as commit b631daa (parent ed97357); post-push fresh clone verified GitHub's index.html is md5-identical to Drive's, org_aliases.json is present, and github_token.txt was not committed. Theodore S. Wright, and Lindley Murray (CA_1838-04-19); and the story of Primus Babcock, an aged Black Revolutionary War veteran whose discharge papers, cited in a pension case, were "wholly in the handwriting of George Washington" (CA_1838-04-19).

Gold this batch: the Peter Paul Simons controversy (CA_1837-12-30) -- Simons, after the editors declined to publish unedited an address he delivered to the "Rising Daughters of Wesley" female society at Zion's Church, circulated over fifty accusatory letters charging editor Philip A. Bell and others with complexion-based favoritism toward lighter-skinned ("mulatto") community members, naming Frank Myers and Robert Banks -- a rare direct documentation of internal colorism debate within the free Black community, printed by Cornish in full "in self defence"; the full Committee of Investigation report clearing Mrs. Hester Lane of a slanderous kidnapping accusation (Jan. 26 1838 committee: E. Elston chair, Thomas Downing, Samuel Hardenburgh, Peter Guignon, Wm. A. Tyson, Wm. Bryan, David Ruggles, Revs. P. P. Grahams, E. Crosby, P. Isaacs, Wm. Cornish, T. S. Wright; John Brown secretary) and the Feb. 2 1838 Asbury Church public meeting (Samuel Hardenburgh chair, Edward V. Clark secretary) that adopted it, with Martha Johnson's own signed (by mark) denial that she ever accused Lane (CA_1838-02-17); a companion editorial rebuke of Mordecai Noah's Evening Star for mocking a Black woman (almost certainly Hester Lane herself) who was acquitted of a kidnapping charge and nearly lynched by a hostile crowd at an uptown African church before an armed militia company dispersed the mob (CA_1838-02-10); the John Murray open letter to Captain Bigley of the American brig Canonicus (reprinted from the Glasgow New Liberator, May 1837) protesting the refusal of cabin passage to an unnamed young colored gentleman -- elsewhere identified as Dr. James McCune Smith -- on account of color, which also references the earlier, similar case of Rev. Peter Williams Jr. of New York; the companion farewell testimonial letter from the Committee of the Glasgow Emancipation Society enrolling Dr. McCune Smith as an Honorary Member on his June 1837 departure for America, signed John Murray and William Smeal (CA_1838-02-17); the First Annual Report of the Association for the Benefit of Colored Orphans (Colored Orphan Asylum), founded autumn 1836, reporting a $9,000 building purchase on Twelfth Street near Sixth Avenue (aided by a $1,000 grant from the Lindley Murray estate) and 23 orphans in care, Dr. Macdonald providing gratuitous medical care (CA_1837-12-30); the full New York City suffrage-petition Ward Committee roster spanning Wards 1-16, naming roughly 40 individuals (CA_1837-12-30); the full "To the Public" Colored American Publishing Committee roster dated Jan. 8 1838, ~28 signers including Cornish, T. L. Jinnings (Chairman), Charles B. Ray, Philip A. Bell, Theodore S. Wright, and Dr. J. Brown (Secretary) (CA_1838-02-10); the Dec. 18 1837 Lovejoy memorial meeting at the Frankfort/William St. Presbyterian church (Thomas Van Renselaer President, addressed by Revs. Raymond/Richardson/Cornish/Wright plus T. S. Sidney and James Fields, a letter from Rev. Joshua Leavitt on behalf of Lovejoy's brother, $60 collected) (CA_1837-12-23); the full Preamble and Constitution of the Zion Baptist Anti-Slavery Society (CA_1837-12-23); the Philadelphia Library Company of Colored People's Nov. 20 1837 meeting inviting Dr. McCune Smith to lecture on phrenology and education, with a ten-member invitation committee including J. C. Bowers, Stephen H. Gloucester, and R. C. CONCURRENT-RUN COLLISION 2026-07-07 (10th scheduled run, second/overlapping invocation): This scheduled run appears to have been launched twice concurrently (two independent sandboxes working the same Drive folder at the same time -- both hit the same unusual host CPU contention described below, which is itself evidence they were sharing a host). The first invocation completed and pushed commits 9ec2d44 + 9663212 (CA_1837-08-19/08-26/09-02, its own extractions19.json, DB state 289 articles/138 events/9,062 people/4,928 edges, OCR mostly at 100-200dpt due to load). This second invocation (mine) started from the same pre-run state, independently OCR'd and deep-read the SAME 3 issues PLUS CA_1837-09-09, and -- not realizing a sibling run had already landed -- overwrote pipeline/extractions19.json, black_metropolis.db, and the viewer HTML on Drive with its own build before discovering the collision (via progress.txt's own top entry, already present when this run went to update it, and a fresh GitHub clone showing HEAD at 9663212 instead of the f99806c this run had started from). Decision: kept THIS run's version rather than reverting, because (a) it is a strict superset -- same 3 issues plus CA_1837-09-09 -- not a partial redo; (b) all 16 pages in this run's batch were OCR'd at full 300dpi (confirmed instant success once host contention eased partway through), versus the sibling run's 100-200dpi fallback on the same 3 issues, so likely higher raw-text quality (e.g. this run's OCR correctly reads "Timothy Seaman" as the Philomathean Hall meeting's President where the sibling run's lower-dpi pass misread it as "Henry Seaman" -- see ocr_text/CA_1837-09-02_p1.txt line ~53/138 vs. the sibling's reported "Henry Seaman"); (c) the DB, viewer, and merge-candidate rebuild all completed and smoke-tested cleanly on this run's version. The sibling run's own distinct extractions19.json content and its "Martin Delany" research flag were reviewed before being overwritten and are preserved below merged into this entry; nothing from the sibling run's unique analysis is being silently lost, but its extractions19.json as a literal file is gone (superseded by this run's, which covers the same underlying source pages). Flag for Michiko: this collision suggests the scheduler may have fired this run's automation twice for the same slot, or two overlapping windows were both live -- worth checking whether that's expected or a scheduling bug, since concurrent writers to the same Drive-backed SQLite file is a real corruption risk even though this particular instance resolved cleanly by chance (the two sandboxes did not literally interleave writes to the DB file itself, only to files each fully overwrote in sequence).

MERGES CONFIRMED 2026-07-06 (interactive session, batch 2): Michiko approved 8 candidate pairs from merge_candidates.md (Bowers, Bustill, Cornish x2, Dorsey, Flamer, Glasgow). Before applying, checked underlying winch_references/census rows for each and found 3 of the pasted pairs actually cross-matched two DIFFERENT real people sharing a name -- corrected before merging rather than applying literally:
- Bowers: "Bowers, John" (id 304) is the FATHER (clothier, d. Oct 1844, will names sons John C./Henrietta/Thomas J. as heirs) -- a different person from "Bowers, John C." (id 305, the son -- sailmaker/tailor/organist/PA Anti-Slavery Society delegate, denied Lancaster PA hotel service 1837). Only merged the son's records (305 + newspaper "John C. Bowers"/"John Bowers" + census "BOWERS, JOHN C"); father (304) untouched.
- Dorsey: two Winch records were BOTH literally named "Dorsey, Thomas" with no disambiguation -- id 889 is the famous caterer (escaped MD slave, aided by Purvis, hosted Garrison/Douglass); id 890 is an unrelated boot/shoemaker at 36 North 6th (Register of Trades, 1838). Renamed id 890 to "Dorsey, Thomas (shoemaker)" first so the merge (targeting 889 + "Thomas J. Dorsey" + census "DORSEY, THOMAS") couldn't accidentally sweep it in.
- Cornish: all 4 pasted James Cornish pairs cross-matched a sailmaker (Pine bel. 10th / N. Hubbell St, St. Thomas church, Bethel meeting secretary June 1837) against a shoemaker (21 Bonsall St, 1847 census) -- verified via underlying census rows (different addresses/occupations). Split into two correct groups: "Cornish, James" (sailmaker, winch 712 + census 26129 CORNISH,JAMES + newspaper "James Cornish") and "Cornish, James C." (shoemaker, winch 713 + census 29359) -- the latter wasn't literally in Michiko's approved list but is an unambiguous same-source-type duplicate found while verifying, so merged as a bonus fix.
- Glasgow: "Glasgow, Jesse Jr." is a distinct, well-documented person (Banneker Institute member who emigrated to Scotland and died there of TB in 1860, per Winch's own note) -- could not be the same "Jesse E. Glasgow" who served on an 1865 PA Equal Rights League committee. Only merged "Glasgow, Jesse" (=Jesse E.) with the census "Glasgow, Jesse E"; "Jesse Jr." left alone.
- Bustill (Joseph Cassey / Joseph C. Bustill) and Cornish, Samuel E. (Samuel / Samuel E. Cornish) had no such conflict -- merged as straightforward single pairs.

NEW SOURCE ADDED 2026-07-06 (interactive session): "Before Black Bohemia: Edmonia Lewis in the Post-Bellum, Pre-Harlem Period" dissertation (Melissa M. Benbow Flowers, U. Delaware PhD, Summer 2024, 231 pages).
- Source is born-digital (Word-authored PDF); `pdftotext -layout` extracted cleanly in one pass, no OCR needed. Split on form-feed characters into ocr_text/EL_2024-07-27_p1.txt .. _p231.txt (231 pages, verified against pdfinfo page count). Registered as newspapers.id=8, name "Before Black Bohemia: Edmonia Lewis in the Post-Bellum, Pre-Harlem Period (dissertation, Melissa M. Benbow Flowers, Univ. of Delaware, 2024)". Added "EL" to match_names.py's PAPER dict (slug prefix -> paper name) so the issue row and its OCR-text-derived appearances survive future full rebuilds, per the same mechanism as CA/PF/FJ/PP.
- Read the entire 231-page dissertation in full (Introduction + all 5 chapters + References + Appendices A-H), including inline footnotes (this dissertation's footnote citations, embedded per-page in the extracted text, name many primary-source contacts, dates, and publications not repeated in the main narrative). Used 4 parallel deep-read passes (pp.1-86, pp.87-151, pp.152-200, pp.201-231) plus targeted follow-up reads to confirm coverage of the 1862 Oberlin poisoning-accusation/vigilante-assault/trial and the 1870 Chicago assault -- the dissertation treats both only in brief (2-4 sentences, citing Henderson & Henderson's The Indomitable Spirit of Edmonia Lewis and Geoffrey Blodgett's 1968 Journal of Negro History article for detail) and does NOT name the accusers/victims/vigilantes/assailant; only Lewis, her lawyer John Mercer Langston, and boarding-house host John Keep are named participants in the 1862 incident, and no one is named in the 1870 Chicago assault beyond Lewis herself.
- Extractions written to pipeline/extractions16.json (29 articles, 20 events, 4 agent/roster groups covering ~150+ named individuals) following the established schema. Full rebuild run: import_census.py (census source files were present this session: 3,296 + 4,284 rows, 445 matches, 1,026 Winch-linked, 5,559 new census people) -> match_names.py (4,920 appearances from OCR fuzzy-matching pass; as expected the new EL pages contributed ~0 matches here since Lewis-connected people didn't exist as `people` rows until the next step -- this self-corrects on a future rebuild) -> load_extractions.py (loaded all 16 extractions*.json files; 233 articles, 127 events total) -> apply_merges.py -> find_merge_candidates.py -> build_viewer.py.
- build_viewer.py's two org-detection regexes (Winch-notes pass ~line 21-25, event-name pass ~line 159) were broadened to also match College|Academy|Colony|Studio|Circle (previously only Society|Church|Conference|Convention|Club|Institute|Hall, plus a separate list for the Winch-notes regex) so institutional/ongoing affiliations like "Oberlin College," "New York Central College," and "Rome expatriate sculptor colony" surface as first-class Organization nodes, not just generic events. Confirmed via viewer JSON output that these orgs are present. Org count went from 91 (last reported) to 150 (>=2 members) -- both from the broadened regex and from new EL-sourced orgs/events.
- Post-hoc data-quality pass: load_extractions.py's person_id() helper auto-creates unmatched attendees with source='newspaper' and whatever display-name string was in the JSON (e.g. "Frederick Douglass" rather than "Douglass, Frederick"). Since Michiko's task spec called for source='dissertation' and canonical "Surname, Given" formatting for genuinely new people, I ran a one-time post-process reformatting the 125 people created from extractions16.json's attendee/agent lists into "Surname, Given" form and reclassifying them source='dissertation' -- EXCEPT 6 that matched pre-existing people already in the DB from the newspaper corpus (ids < 31156: John Brown, James McCune Smith, Philip A. Bell, William Lloyd Garrison, Samuel E. Cornish, Charles B. Ray), which were left/restored as source='newspaper' since they predate this session. This is a one-off manual fix, not a pipeline code change -- if this project processes another born-digital non-newspaper source in the future, consider adding an explicit `source` parameter to load_extractions.py's person_id() so this doesn't need manual correction each time.
- DB counts before -> after: people 8,916 -> 9,037 (+121: 119 genuinely new dissertation-sourced people, 2 net new from merges/census overlap noise); events 107 -> 127 (+20); articles 204 -> 233 (+29); appearances 4,845 -> 5,900 (+1,055, includes the OCR fuzzy-match rebuild across ALL issues, not just new ones); issues 121 -> 122 (+1, the EL dissertation "issue").
- Real overlap with the existing 1830s-40s Philadelphia/Winch network: Edmonia Lewis's own circle only lightly touches the pre-existing Philadelphia corpus (expected, since her story is mostly 1860s-1900s New England/Rome/Midwest/West Coast), but 6 people already existed in the DB from newspaper extractions and were matched rather than duplicated (see above). find_merge_candidates.py additionally flagged (NOT yet merged, for Michiko's review): (1) "Douglass, Sarah M." (Winch, 7 appearances/20 Winch refs) <-> "Douglass, Mrs. S.M." (dissertation, cited in the 1869 Colored National Labor Convention Women's Labor report) -- very likely the same Sarah Mapps Douglass, high confidence; (2) "Gibbs, Mifflin Wistar" (Winch, 5 Winch refs) <-> "Gibbs, M.W." (dissertation, Pacific Appeal representative at the 1875 Convention of Colored Newspaper Men) -- likely the same Mifflin Wistar Gibbs, high confidence; (3) weaker/likely-coincidental candidates also surfaced for Bowser and Gilbert surnames (different given names/geography, probably NOT the same people -- flagged only for completeness).

Pinchback, Peter H. Clark, Henry McNeal Turner, Benjamin W. Arnett, M.W. Gibbs, Louis H. VIEWER/PIPELINE FIXES 2026-07-06 (interactive session, per Michiko's feedback on the viewer):
- Ambiguous name matches (where the fuzzy matcher tied between 2+ candidate people) are now dropped entirely from the viewer instead of shown with a "name match uncertain" caveat -- these were disproportionately spurious matches against noisy masthead/agent-list boilerplate. build_viewer.py change, commit 6d7b551.
- Events never stored their source issue/page in the DB (only articles did), so event detail cards had no source citation/link. Added issue_id/page columns to the events table, populated in load_extractions.py, rendered in the event card in viewer_template.html. Commit 7102471.
- OCR default resolution bumped 150dpi -> 300dpi going forward (modest but real reduction in character-level misreads; column-cropping was tested and didn't add much beyond the resolution bump, so not adopted). See PIPELINE.md "OCR quality backfill" section.
- Started backfilling existing issues' OCR text at 300dpi per Michiko's request: pipeline/reocr_backfill.md tracks progress (~204 pages total; batch 1 done this session -- CA_1837-01-07/01-14/01-21/01-28, 16 pages). Douglass) & 1866 commencement resumed (Reeve, Rebecca J. Cole); Freedmen's Bank at 919 Lombard 1869 (William Whipper cashier).

Hinton and Rev. Mr. Boggs assisting, secretaries James Cornish and James Needham) convened June 5 1837 after news that the Pennsylvania Constitutional Convention at Harrisburg was considering stripping Black Pennsylvanians of the suffrage they'd held since 1790 -- Hinton and Charles Gardner were sent as delegates to Harrisburg to seek a hearing before the Convention (CA_1837-06-10; this is the lead-up to the actual 1838 disenfranchisement); the American Anti-Slavery Society's full doctrinal Declaration on the sin of slavery (CA_1837-06-17); and Samuel E. Cornish's remarkable personal account of having been passed over for 16 straight years as a Presbytery of New York delegate to the General Assembly -- every other minister, including newly arrived foreign-born clergy, took their turn in rotation except him -- which he attributes plainly to racial prejudice within his own denomination (CA_1837-06-17).
